## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species concentration over time. In reaction kinetics, dA/dt is typically governed by rate laws that depend on concentration A (and occasionally explicitly on time for non-elementary or externally driven reactions).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (approach to equilibrium)
- Mixed-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (parallel first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant)
- Consecutive reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (intermediate species dynamics)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with background rate)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type rate law)
- Parallel pathways: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**c2 + c3 (multiple simultaneous reaction channels)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit t) → autonomous ODE rate law, suggesting elementary or pseudo-elementary reaction mechanism
- Negative proportionality to A → consumption/decay reaction where species A is a reactant
- Product of A and (constant - A) → autocatalytic or logistic growth behavior typical of self-catalyzing reactions
- Rational function of A (numerator/denominator polynomial) → enzyme kinetics or surface-catalyzed reactions with adsorption-desorption equilibrium
- Integer power of A (A², A³) → molecularity of reaction corresponds to number of molecules in elementary step
- Explicit time dependence alongside A → non-autonomous system such as photolysis with varying light intensity or temperature ramp experiments
- Sum of terms with different powers of A → competing parallel reaction pathways with different orders
- Concentration raised to non-integer power → apparent fractional order from complex mechanism or diffusion-limited kinetics
- Sign of dA/dt changing at specific A values → equilibrium point where forward and reverse reaction rates balance
- Rate proportional to A times exponential of time → effective rate constant changing due to catalyst deactivation or temperature programming
